The Prophet's Call: Proof, Gradual Education, and Global Spread
Ibn Asakir describes the Prophet's call, proof, and gradual education.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Prophet established rational proof for his call, educated people gradually in beliefs and morals, and how his message spread globally in a short time.

Core Idea
The Prophet's call combined rational proof, gradual education, and universal reach.

Ibn Asakir invites us to reflect on the Prophet's extraordinary method of calling to Islam amid a corrupted world. He not only left no excuse for the obstinate but also awakened minds in a way that both commoners and elites could accept. This lesson explores the Prophet's approach: establishing proof, teaching transcendence and virtue, and the eventual global spread of his Sharia.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage context
Note that the passage begins by describing the state of the region at the time of the Prophet's mission, setting the stage for his call.
2
Identify the key aspects of the Prophet's method
Look for how the Prophet established proof, awakened minds, taught tanzih and fiqh, and urged gradual progress.
3
Reflect on the global expansion
Consider how the Prophet's Sharia broke through its original sphere and spread to all horizons, benefiting the world in a short time.
4
Connect to the lesson's theme
Understand that this passage highlights the systematic and miraculous nature of the Prophet's mission, which is a sign of his prophethood.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وهكذا كان الحجاز وما حوله من فلسطين والشام وبلاد الروم والعراق وأرض الفرس والهند وبلاد افريقية وما والاها حين بعث النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم فانظر يارعاك الله كيف قام هذا النبي الكريم بالدعوة إلى الإسلام في هذا الوسط بين تلك الملل المحيطة به ثم كيف اقام الحجة لدعوته بحيث لا يدع لمعاند عذرا وكيف أيقظ العقول بطريقة لا تعلو عن مدارك العامة ولا يستنكرها الخاصة فدانوا له تباعا وعلمهم طريق التنزيه وما يجوز في الله وما لا يجوز، وفقههم فى أبواب العمل ودربهم على الفضيلة والسجايا الكريمة واستنهض الجميع نحو رقى مستمر في العلوم والأعمال والأخلاق وما إليها استنهاضا تدريجيا بعيدا عن الطفرة والمفاجأة، ثم كيف خرق شرعه هذا النطاق وانتشر إلى جميع الآفاق فدانت الأمم بنور هدايته في مشارق الأرض ومغاربها، ثم كيف أفاضت هذه الدعوة المباركة والنهضة الميمونة على العالمين مالم يعهد له مثيل من الخيرات في أيسر مدة، فإذا تأملت ذلك تزداد يقينا وترى في ثنايا تشريع هذا النبي العظيم معجزات أية معجزات تتجدد مدى الدهر وأمهات ما تلقت الأمة من النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم هي العلم بالله وصفاته وما إليها من المعتقدات المقصودة لذاتها، والعلم بالأحكام العملية من عبادات ومعاملات يدور عليها تهذيبهم النفسي وإقامة العدل بين الخليقة والعلم بطرق اكتساب الملكات الفاضلة والتخلي عن الخلال الرديئة النفسية، مما يرشد إلى وسائل تزكية النفوس وتصفية القلوب، حتى تصدر منها الأعمال المسعدة في النشأتين سجية لا بتكليف فيتم لهم الكمالات العلمية والعملية وكان الصحابة رضى الله عنهم في غنية عن تدوين تلك العلوم لأنهم كانوا يرجعون إلى النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم إذا اشتبهوا في أمر فيزول الأشكال ويحصل العلم ويأنسون به في الأعمال، ويسعون في التخلق بخلقه العظيم، فلا يتنكبون العدل في
Thus was the Hijaz and its surroundings of Palestine, Syria, the lands of Rome, Iraq, the land of Persia, India, the lands of Africa, and what adjoins them at the time when the Prophet, may God bless him and grant him peace, was sent. So look, may God preserve you, how this noble Prophet undertook the call to Islam in this midst among those surrounding religions, then how he established the proof for his call such that he left no excuse for the obstinate, and how he awakened minds in a way that does not rise above the understanding of the common people nor is rejected by the elite; so they submitted to him one after another. He taught them the way of transcendence (tanzih) and what is permissible regarding God and what is not; he gave them fiqh in the chapters of action; trained them in virtue and noble qualities; and urged everyone toward continuous progress in sciences, deeds, and morals – a gradual urging far from leaps and surprises. Then how his Sharia broke through this sphere and spread to all horizons, so that nations submitted to the light of his guidance in the east and west of the earth. Then how this blessed call and auspicious renaissance poured forth upon the worlds such good as had never been known in the shortest time. If you reflect on that, you increase in certainty and see within the legislation of this great Prophet miracles – what miracles! – that are renewed throughout time. The mother sciences that the community received from the Prophet, may God bless him and grant him peace, are: knowledge of God and His attributes and what pertains to that of beliefs intended for their own sake; knowledge of practical rulings of worship and transactions around which revolves their psychological refinement and the establishment of justice among creation; and knowledge of the ways to acquire virtuous dispositions and abandon evil psychological traits, which guides to means of purifying souls and cleansing hearts, so that from them issue deeds that bring happiness in both abodes as a natural disposition, not through burden, thus completing for them intellectual and practical perfections. The Companions, may God be pleased with them, were in no need of codifying those sciences because they would refer to the Prophet, may God bless him and grant him peace, if they were uncertain about a matter, so the ambiguity would be removed and knowledge would be attained, and they would become familiar with it in deeds, and they strove to adopt his great character, so they did not deviate from justice in...
Source pages p. 18

Commentary
This passage presents the Prophet's mission as a comprehensive response to the corrupt world described earlier. Ibn Asakir begins with a summary statement: the Hijaz and its surroundings were in the described state when the Prophet was sent. Then he calls the reader to reflect on several aspects. First, how the Prophet called to Islam amidst these surrounding nations, establishing rational proof that left no excuse for anyone. Second, how he awakened minds in a manner accessible to both commoners and elites, leading people to accept Islam gradually. Third, he taught them the principle of tanzih (transcendence of God), distinguishing what is permissible to attribute to God from what is not. Fourth, he taught fiqh (practical rulings) and trained them in virtue and noble character, urging gradual progress in knowledge, deeds, and morals. Fifth, his Sharia broke through its original sphere and spread globally, blessing the world with unprecedented good in a short time. Ibn Asakir then highlights that reflecting on this increases certainty and reveals ongoing miracles within the Prophet's legislation. He then identifies the three 'mother sciences' (ummahat) received from the Prophet: (1) knowledge of God and His attributes – theology (aqidah), (2) knowledge of practical rulings – fiqh (worship and transactions), which serve psychological refinement and justice, and (3) knowledge of ways to acquire virtuous dispositions and purify the soul – tazkiyah (spiritual purification). The goal is that good deeds become natural, not forced, leading to perfection in knowledge and practice. Finally, Ibn Asakir notes that the Companions did not need to codify these sciences because they could directly consult the Prophet whenever uncertain, and they strove to embody his character, thus they did not deviate from justice. The passage is partly descriptive and partly hortatory, urging the reader to recognize the comprehensiveness and miraculous nature of the Prophet's mission.

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's mission combined rational proof, gradual education, and universal reach, leaving no excuse for anyone.

?
The Prophet taught tanzih, fiqh, virtue, and urged gradual progress. Which of these areas is most neglected in your own spiritual growth? What small step can you take today to begin improving in that area?

Life of Imam Ibn Asakir

The Three Mother Sciences and the Companions' Direct Access
Ibn Asakir lists the three mother sciences and the Companions' direct learning.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the three foundational sciences taught by the Prophet (knowledge of God, practical rulings, and spiritual purification) and why the Companions did not need to codify them initially.

Core Idea
The Prophet taught three sciences: theology, law, and spiritual purification; Companions relied on direct consultation.

Ibn Asakir now enumerates the mother sciences brought by the Prophet: knowledge of God and His attributes, practical rulings of worship and transactions, and the ways to acquire virtuous dispositions. These three form the complete system of Islam. He also explains that the Companions were initially in no need of codification because they could refer directly to the Prophet whenever uncertain, being immersed in his character.

Guided Path
1
Read the enumeration of the three sciences
Identify the three categories: knowledge of God (theology), knowledge of practical rulings (fiqh), and knowledge of spiritual purification (tazkiyah).
2
Understand their purpose
Notice that each science serves a purpose: theology for correct belief, fiqh for justice and refinement, tazkiyah for virtuous character.
3
Consider the Companions' situation
Reflect on why the Companions did not need to write down these sciences: they had direct access to the Prophet and were immersed in his character.
4
Appreciate the completeness
Recognize that these three sciences together cover all aspects of life: belief, action, and character.

The Chains of Mu'tazili Scholars
Ibn Asakir lists major Mu'tazili scholars with their transmission chains.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two main scholarly lineages of the Mu'tazila (Basran and Baghdadi) and the key figures in each chain.

Core Idea
Mu'tazilism spread through two distinct chains: one from Basra and one from Baghdad.

In this passage, Ibn Asakir provides a biographical map of the Mu'tazila, showing how the school branched into two geographical centers. By tracing the teachers and students, we see the intellectual genealogy that shaped Mu'tazili thought. Pay attention to the correction Ibn Asakir makes about Ibn Abi Du'ad—a detail that shows his care for historical accuracy.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then read the literal translation. Let the names and relationships sink in.
Notice the two starting points: Bishr and Abu l-Hudhayl.
2
Identify the two main chains
The passage presents two chains: one from Abu l-Hudhayl (Basran) and one from Bishr (Baghdadi). Find the names that belong to each chain.
Hint: Words like 'وعن الأول' and 'وعنهما' help separate them.
3
Note the correction about Ibn Abi Du'ad
Ibn Asakir states that Ibn Abi Du'ad did not meet Wasil, contrary to common belief. Understand why this correction matters for the history of Mu'tazilism.
4
Reflect on the significance
Consider why Ibn Asakir includes this list. It establishes the authority of the Mu'tazila by showing their scholarly pedigrees, and it distinguishes the Basran and Baghdadi schools.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وعنهما أخذ بشر بن المعتمر وأبو الهذيل وبالثاني تخرج أبو بكر عبدالرحمن بن كيسان الأصم وإبراهيم النظام وهشام الفوطى وعلى بن محمد الشحام وعن النظام أخذ الجاحظ وابن أبي دؤاد - ولم يدرك واصلا كما ظن - وعن الأول انتشر الاعتزال ببغداد حيث اخذ منه أبو موسى بن صبيح وعنه جعفر بن حرب وجعفر بن مبشر وعنهما محمد بن عبد الله الاسكافى وعن الشحام أخذ الجبائي وعنه ابنه أبو هاشم، وأخذ عن الفوطى عباد بن سليمان فهؤلاء هم قادة الاعتزال في البصرة وبغداد
And from them (i.e., 'Amr and Bishr) Bishr ibn al-Mu'tamir and Abu l-Hudhayl took (knowledge). From the second (Abu l-Hudhayl) graduated Abu Bakr 'Abdurrahman ibn Kaysan al-Asamm, Ibrahim an-Nazzam, Hisham al-Fuwati, and 'Ali ibn Muhammad ash-Shahham. From an-Nazzam, al-Jahiz and Ibn Abi Du'ad took—he did not meet Wasil, as is thought. From the first (Bishr), i'tizal spread in Baghdad, as Abu Musa ibn Subayh took from him, and from him Ja'far ibn Harb and Ja'far ibn Mubashshir, and from them Muhammad ibn 'Abdullah al-Iskafi. From ash-Shahham, al-Jubba'i took, and from him his son Abu Hashim. And from al-Fuwati, 'Abbad ibn Sulayman took. These are the leaders of i'tizal in Basra and Baghdad.
Source pages p. 21

Commentary
This passage is a biographical list tracing the scholarly lineages of the Mu'tazila. It identifies two main chains: one through Abu l-Hudhayl (Basran school) and one through Bishr ibn al-Mu'tamir (Baghdadi school). Key names include an-Nazzam, al-Jahiz, al-Jubba'i, and others. The note that Ibn Abi Du'ad never met Wasil is a correction of a common misconception. The passage serves to establish the intellectual pedigree of the Mu'tazila and their geographical centers.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
This lesson shows that even within a single theological movement there were distinct chains of transmission and different schools. Have you ever assumed that everyone who shares a label (e.g., 'Muslim,' 'Sunni,' 'Sufi') is uniform in belief and practice? Where did that assumption come from, and how might it lead to injustice against those who are different? Will you commit to asking about a person's specific teachers and sources before making judgments about their faith?
?

Do you cling to the error or humbly accept the correction? Is your love of being right stronger than your love of truth?
?
The scholars in this list invested years seeking knowledge from specific teachers, preserving chains that defined their theology. If not, why are you comfortable with that ignorance, and what step will you take this week to trace your own intellectual lineage?

Life of Imam Ibn Asakir
intermediate
8 min
Jahm's Views and the Spread of Atheism under al-Mahdi
Ibn Asakir discusses Jahm's attributed views and al-Mahdi's commission of refutations against atheists.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Jahm's views were attributed without a distinct sect, and how al-Mahdi responded to the spread of atheism by commissioning refutations from mutakallimun.

Core Idea
Jahm had no followers, but his name became a label for slander amidst rising atheism.

Ibn Asakir begins by clarifying the status of Jahm’s attributed views, noting that no sect continued under his name and that most attributions are slanders. He then describes a critical historical shift: as conquests slowed, people turned to speculative thought, and atheists like Ibn al-Muqaffa‘ and others spread their ideas. This prompted Caliph al-Mahdi to order the mutakallimun to write refutations, thereby defending the faith. This lesson anchors the importance of caliphal support for theology in the face of ideological threats.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the literal translation. Note the flow from Jahm's attributed views to al-Mahdi's response.
The footnote about 'Abd al-Karim is integrated; notice how it illustrates the problem of fabricated hadith.
2
Identify the two main themes
The passage has two parts: first, the nature of Jahm's attributed views; second, the rise of atheism and al-Mahdi's reaction. Distinguish them.
3
Examine the key figures
List the individuals mentioned: Jahm, Ibn al-Muqaffa', Hammad 'Ajrad, etc. Their roles show the movement of ideas.
This helps connect the historical narrative to theological reactions.
4
Reflect on the caliph's role
Al-Mahdi ordered mutakallimun to write refutations. Ask yourself why the state intervened in theological matters.
Consider the political and religious motives behind commissioning scholarly works.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وتنسب لجهم آراء وليس له فرقة تنتمى إليه بعده ونسبة غالب من نسب إليه من قبيل النبذ بالألقاب تهويلا لسوء سمعه الرجل بين الفرق وآراؤه توزعت بينهم بعد تمحيصها على حسب انظارهم لا على ما ارتآه جهم شأن كل رأى يشيع في الناس . وبعد أن ابتدأ يطرأ بعض فتور على الفتوح ازداد الناس تفرغا لتلك الآراء المبثوثة، وتغلب على عقولهم شهوة التعمق فيها وأخد أمثال ابن المقفع وحماد عجرد ويحيى بن زياد ومطيع بن اياس وعبد الكريم بن أبى العوجاء (١) يواصلون السعى فى نشر الالحاد بين المسلمين وترجمة كتب الملاحدة والثنوية من الفرس حتى استفحل أمرهم، فأمر المهدى علماء المتكلمين بتصنيف الكتب في الرد على الملحدين، فأقاموا الجدل من البراهين وأزالوا الشبه وأوضحوا الحق وخدموا الدين.
(١) كان ربيب حماد بن سلمة وكان اعترف انه وضع أربعة آلاف حديث . وقد راج ما دس منها في كتب ابيه لأمه بعدما خرف بين كثير من الرواة ثم صارت حججا يتمسك بها الحشوية في معتقدهم.
And views are attributed to Jahm, and he has no sect that follows him after him. The attribution of most of those who attribute to him is of the type of slander with labels, exaggerating his bad reputation among the sects. His views were distributed among them after being examined according to their opinions, not according to what Jahm himself held, as is the case with every view that spreads among people. After some slackening began to appear in the conquests, people became more at leisure to engage in those scattered views, and the desire for delving into them overcame their minds. And the likes of Ibn al-Muqaffa', Hammad 'Ajrad, Yahya ibn Ziyad, Muti' ibn Iyas, and 'Abd al-Karim ibn Abi al-'Awja' continued striving to spread atheism among Muslims and translating the books of the atheists and the dualists from the Persians, until their matter became severe. So al-Mahdi ordered the mutakallim scholars to compose books in refutation of the atheists, so they set up debate from proofs, removed doubts, clarified the truth, and served the religion. (He was the foster child of Hammad ibn Salama, and he admitted that he fabricated four thousand hadiths. And what was smuggled from them into the books of his maternal father became widespread after he became senile among many of the narrators, then they became arguments that the Hashwiyya cling to in their creed.)
Source pages p. 22

Commentary
This passage first addresses the attribution of views to Jahm, noting that no real sect continued under his name after him, and that most attributions are slanders rather than accurate reports. It then describes a historical shift: as the early conquests slowed, people had more time to delve into speculative views. Figures like Ibn al-Muqaffa' and 'Abd al-Karim ibn Abi al-'Awja' actively worked to spread atheism (ilhad) and translate atheist and dualist works from Persian. This prompted the caliph al-Mahdi to commission mutakallimun—theologians—to write refutations. These scholars produced arguments, removed doubts, and defended the religion. The footnote (marked ١) identifies 'Abd al-Karim ibn Abi al-'Awja' as a notorious hadith fabricator who claimed to have fabricated four thousand hadiths, and notes that these fabrications entered books used by the Hashwiyya as proof texts.

ilhad
zindeeq
mutakallimun
al-Mahdi
Hashwiyya

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Jahm founded a distinct sect that continued after him.
Correction: Ibn Asakir states: 'And views are attributed to Jahm, and he has no sect that follows him after him.' The attributions are often slanderous labels, not accurate representations of a continuous school.

Checkpoint
According to Ibn Asakir, what action did al-Mahdi take in response to the spread of atheism?
A) He imprisoned the atheists
B) He ordered mutakallimun to write refutation books
C) He banned translation of foreign works
D) He exiled the atheists

Key Takeaway
Jahm had no enduring sect; the spread of atheism under al-Mahdi prompted state-sponsored theological refutations by mutakallimun.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever attributed a belief to someone—like 'Jahmi', 'Mu'tazili', or 'liberal'—without truly verifying what they hold? What would it take for you to stop using labels as slander and instead seek the truth from their own words?
?
The mutakallimun wrote refutations because atheism was spreading. If you saw falsehood undermining your community today, would you have the knowledge and courage to respond with proofs, or would you remain silent? What is one step you can take this week to learn how to defend your faith?
?
Ibn Abi al-'Awja' fabricated thousands of hadith to support his agenda. Are there any opinions you hold that rest on questionable sources—perhaps something you heard without checking? Will you examine the foundation of your beliefs, even if it is uncomfortable?

Spread of Ash'arism After al-Ash'ari's Death
Describes how Ash'arism spread after al-Ash'ari's death through al-Baqillani's efforts.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Ash'ari school spread through the efforts of al-Baqillani and his disciples to North Africa, Sicily, and Andalusia.

Core Idea
Al-Baqillani and his students carried Ash'arism from Iraq to the far Maghrib.

After al-Ash'ari's death, the Mu'tazila briefly resurged under the Buwayhids, but the scholar al-Baqillani decisively defeated them. He then orchestrated a systematic spread of Ash'arism by sending his disciples to key regions, from Syria to North Africa, and eventually to Sicily and Andalusia. This passage from Ibn 'Asakir's work highlights the geographical expansion of the school.

Commentary

Al-Baqillani sent one of his companions, Abu 'Abdallah al-Husayn al-Azdi, to Syria, then to Qayrawan and the Maghrib. This led to the adherence of the Maghribi scholars to the Ash'ari school, which then spread to Sicily and Andalusia. The passage ends by mentioning Ibn Abi Zayd (al-Qayrawani) and Abu 'Imran al-Fasi, two prominent Maghribi Malikis associated with Ash'arism. The text continues but the page ends here. This passage shows the geographical expansion of the Ash'ari school through the efforts of al-Baqillani and his disciples.

The Historical Crisis and Al-Ash'ari's Reconciliatory Approach
Describes the sectarian turmoil and al-Ash'ari's initial reconciliatory approach.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the sectarian turmoil before Imam al-Ash'ari and his initial strategy of reconciliation to restore the middle path.

Core Idea
Al-Ash'ari first sought reconciliation, not confrontation.

This lesson sets the stage for Imam al-Ash'ari's emergence. At a time of deep sectarian strife, with the Mu'tazila gaining intellectual dominance and heretics spreading corruption, al-Ash'ari stepped forward. His first move was not to attack but to reconcile the warring factions and bring them back to the balanced middle way.

Guided Path
1
Read the historical passage
Read the Arabic passage once, then its translation. Let the narrative of crisis and response sink in before analysis.
The language is dense; take your time.
2
Identify the actors and their roles
List the groups mentioned: Mu'tazila, atheists, Qarmatians. What was each doing? The Mu'tazila dominated scholars' minds, atheists/Qarmatians occupied lands.
These groups represent theological and political threats.
3
Understand the severity of the crisis
The text says no one was left to defend with conclusive proofs. Why? Because defenders were occupied with themselves. Grasp the urgency.
This vacuum sets the stage for al-Ash'ari.
4
Analyze al-Ash'ari's initial response
He felt grief, stood for Sunnah against innovation, but first sought reconciliation between factions to bring them to the middle. This is key.
Reconciliation was not weakness; it was strategic.
5
Reflect on the 'just middle' concept
Consider why the middle way is a defining feature of Sunni orthodoxy. This theme will recur in later lessons.
The middle way avoids extremes of both sides.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وليس هذا محل بسط مخازيهم. وكانت المعتزلة تتغلب على عقول المفكرين من العلماء ويسعون فى استعادة سلطانهم على الأمة وأصناف الملاحدة والقرامطة توغلوا فى الفساد واحتلوا البلاد حيث لم يبق في ثغور الدفاع عن الدين من يرابط بحجج دامغة تمحق مخرقتهم لانشغالهم بنفوسهم بما جد من الأحوال. ففى مثل هذه الظروف الحرجة غار الامام أبو الحسن الأشعرى رضى الله عنه على ما حل بالمسلمين من ضروب النكال وقام لنصرة السنة وقمع البدعة فسعى أولاً للاصلاح بين الفريقين من الأمة بارجاعهما عن تطرفهما إلى الوسط العدل.
This is not the place to detail their abuses. The Mu'tazila dominated the minds of intellectuals among the scholars and sought to restore their authority over the ummah, and various groups of atheists and Qarmatians delved into corruption and occupied lands, such that there remained in the frontiers of defense of the religion no one holding firm with conclusive proofs that would destroy their fraud, due to their being occupied with themselves by what had newly occurred of circumstances. So in such critical conditions, Imam Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari, may Allah be pleased with him, was moved by what had befallen the Muslims of various kinds of affliction, and he stood to support the Sunnah and suppress innovation. He first sought reconciliation between the two factions of the ummah by bringing them back from their extremism to the just middle.
Source pages p. 24

Commentary
This passage provides historical context. It describes a time of severe sectarian strife: the Mu'tazila were intellectually dominant and seeking political power, while heretics and Qarmatians were causing chaos. The defenders of orthodoxy were weak. In response, Imam al-Ash'ari emerged to defend the Sunnah and combat innovation. His first approach was not confrontation but reconciliation: he tried to bring the two extreme factions (likely the Mu'tazila and the anthropomorphists or other groups) back to the middle way. This sets the stage for his later detailed positions.

Correction: The text shows his first approach was reconciliation to bring factions to the middle, not partisanship.

Key Takeaway
Imam al-Ash'ari responded to a severe sectarian crisis by first seeking reconciliation to restore the just middle way.

The Spread of Ash'arism After al-Ash'ari
Chronicles the dissemination of Ash'ari doctrine through al-Baqillani and his students.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Ash'ari school was disseminated after al-Ash'ari's death, particularly through the efforts of Imam al-Baqillani and his students.

Core Idea
The Ash'ari school spread through scholarly networks, not political power alone.

After the death of Imam al-Ash'ari, his teachings continued to spread through his students and their works. However, the Mu'tazila briefly regained strength under the Buwayhids. It was Imam Abu Bakr al-Baqillani who rose to defend the Ash'ari creed and systematically dispatched scholars to propagate it across North Africa, Sicily, and Andalusia. This passage traces that remarkable expansion.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then its translation. Notice the sequence of events: Ash'ari's fame, his death, Mu'tazila revival, al-Baqillani's response, and the dispatch of scholars.
The passage flows chronologically.

Identify the key figures mentioned
Make a list of the scholars named: al-Baqillani, al-Azdi, Ibn Abi Zayd, etc. Think about their roles.
3
Reflect on the method of dissemination
Consider how al-Baqillani used personal student networks and scholarly correspondence to spread the school. What does this say about the transmission of knowledge in pre-modern Islam?
This connects to the core idea.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وتواردت عليه المسائل من اقطار العالم فاجاب عنها فطبق ذكره الآفاق وملاء العالم بكتبه وكتب اصحابه في السنة والرد على اصناف المبتدعة والملاحدة وأهل الكتاب وتفرق أصحابه في بلاد العراق وخرسان والشام وبلاد المغرب ومضى لسبيله، وبعد وفاته بيسير استعاد المعتزلة بعض قوتهم في عهد بني بويه لكن الامام ناصر السنة أبا بكر بن الباقلاني قام في وجههم وقمعهم بحججه ودانت للسنة على الطريقة الاشعرية أهل البسيطة الى اقصى بلاد افريقية وقد بعث ابن الباقلاني في جملة من بعث من أصحابه الى البلاد ابا عبدالله الحسين بن عبدالله بن حاتم الازدي الى الشام، ثم الى قيروان وبلاد المغرب فدان له أهل العلم من أئمة المغاربة وانتشر المذهب الى صقلية والاندلس ولابن ابى زيد وأبي عمران الفاسي وابي الحسن القابسي وابى الوليد بن الباجي وأبي بكر بن العربي تلامذتهم أياد بيضاء في ذلك.
Questions came to him from all parts of the world, and he answered them, such that his fame filled the horizons and his books and the books of his companions filled the world concerning the Sunnah and refutation of various innovators, atheists, and People of the Book. His companions dispersed in the lands of Iraq, Khurasan, Syria, and the lands of the Maghrib, and he passed on. Shortly after his death, the Mu'tazila regained some strength in the era of the Buwayhids, but the supporter of the Sunnah, Abu Bakr ibn al-Baqillani, stood against them and suppressed them with his proofs, and the people of the entire earth up to the farthest lands of Africa adhered to the Sunnah upon the Ash'ari way. Ibn al-Baqillani sent, among those he dispatched from his companions to the lands, Abu 'Abdallah al-Husayn ibn 'Abdallah ibn Hatim al-Azdi to Syria, then to Qayrawan and the lands of the Maghrib, so the people of knowledge among the Maghribi imams adhered to him, and the school spread to Sicily and Andalusia. Ibn Abi Zayd, Abu 'Imran al-Fasi, Abu al-Hasan al-Qabisi, Abu al-Walid al-Baji, and Abu Bakr ibn al-'Arabi — their students — had white hands (i.e., praiseworthy efforts) in that.
Source pages p. 24

Commentary
This passage narrates the propagation of the Ash'ari school after the death of its founder. During his lifetime, Ash'ari's works spread globally. After his death, the Mu'tazila briefly revived under the Buwayhids, but Ibn al-Baqillani emerged as a champion, defeating them and re-establishing Ash'arism across vast territories. His method included sending scholars like Ibn Hatim al-Azdi to various regions, resulting in the adoption of Ash'arism by the leading imams of the Maghrib, and further expansion into Sicily and Andalusia. The passage lists several notable figures who contributed to this spread, highlighting their praiseworthy efforts.

Early Spread of Ash'arism in Hijaz and Syria
Describes early spread of Ash'arism via Abu Dharr and al-Tabari.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Ash'arism was initially disseminated in the Hijaz and Syria through the efforts of Abu Dharr al-Harawi and 'Abd al-'Aziz al-Tabari.

Core Idea
Ash'arism spread through scholar networks, not state power.

This lesson traces the early spread of Ash'arism in the Islamic heartlands. We see how two key transmitters played pivotal roles: Abu Dharr al-Harawi in the Hijaz and 'Abd al-'Aziz al-Tabari in Syria. Their efforts laid the foundation for the school's later prominence.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on early spread
Read the Arabic passage and its translation, focusing on the two scholars named.
Notice how both are described as transmitters (rawiya) of major works.
2
Identify the geographical scope
The passage mentions Hijaz and Syria. Reflect on why these regions were important for Ash'arism.
The Hijaz was home to Mecca and Medina; Syria was a center of Islamic learning.
3
Consider the method of spread
The passage says scholars traveled to Abu Dharr and that al-Tabari was a companion of al-Ash'ari. What does this tell us about the early transmission of the school?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقام بنشر المذهب في الحجاز راوية الجامع الصحيح الحافظ ابو ذر الهروى وأخذ عنه من ارتحل اليه من علماء الآفاق، وكان انتشاره بالشام قبل ذلك بواسطة صاحب الاشعری ابی الحسن عبد العزيز الطبري راوية تفسير ابن جرير عن مؤلفه وكان اهل الشام يجتلبون عبـار الائمة من المذهب الأشعرى حيناً بعد حين كالامام قطب الدين النيسابورى اجتلبه نور الدين الشهيد على طلب العلماء. وكان جماعة من المقادسة الحنابلة ممن ورثوا بعض آراء ابن كرام الذى كان عشش بالقدس وباض وترك أصحابا له متقشفين يتوارثها منهم من بعدهم هاجروا منها لما احتلها النصارى وحملوا بدع التشبيه الى الشام وكان بها شئ من تلك البدع من عهد عبد الواحد الشيرازي صاحب أبي يعلى وكان السلطان صلاح الدين الايوبى يرعى خاطرهم لكونهم مهاجرين زهادا ويتغاضى عن معتقدهم، ولم يكن يحمل الناس علي المذهب الأشعرى كما ظن بل كان الواعظ ابن نجية الحنبلى المشهور مقربا عنده ومجافاته القاسية مع الامام الشهاب الطوسى القائم بنصرة الاشعرى بمصر تجرى على منظر منه ومسمع ويسكت عن ذلك بل كاد آله أن ينحازوا اليهم فى المعتقد لولا وقفة الأمام عز الدين بن عبد السلام فى هذه المسألة وقفة عالم يقوم بواجبه فتضاءات أصواتهم وانجمعوا في ديورهم واقتصروا على الروايات.
The spreader of the school in the Hijaz was the transmitter of the Sahih, the hafiz Abu Dharr al-Harawi, and those who traveled to him from the scholars of the regions learned from him. Its spread in Syria before that was through the companion of al-Ash'ari, Abu al-Hasan 'Abd al-'Aziz al-Tabari, the transmitter of the Tafsir of Ibn Jarir from its author. The people of Syria would import imams of the Ash'ari school from time to time, such as Imam Qutb al-Din al-Naysaburi, who was brought by Nur al-Din al-Shahid at the request of scholars. There was a group of the Muqaddasa Hanbalis who had inherited some views of Ibn Karram, who had nested in Jerusalem and bred and left ascetic followers, which they inherited from one another. They emigrated from there when the Christians occupied it and carried the innovations of anthropomorphism to Syria. There was some of that innovation in Syria from the time of 'Abd al-Wahid al-Shirazi, the companion of Abu Ya'la. Sultan Salah al-Din al-Ayyubi would consider their feelings because they were emigrants and ascetics, and he overlooked their creed. He did not compel people to follow the Ash'ari school as was thought. Rather, the preacher Ibn Najiyya al-Hanbali was close to him. And his harsh disassociation with Imam Shihab al-Tusi, who stood for the support of Ash'arism in Egypt, occurred in his sight and hearing, and he remained silent about it. Indeed, his family almost inclined towards them in creed, had it not been for the stance of Imam 'Izz al-Din ibn 'Abd al-Salam on this issue—a stance of a scholar fulfilling his duty. Then their voices faded, and they confined themselves to their homes and restricted themselves to narrations.
Source pages p. 25

Commentary
This passage continues the historical narrative, focusing on the Levant. It mentions Abu Dharr al-Harawi spreading the school in the Hijaz and 'Abd al-'Aziz al-Tabari in Syria earlier. Nur al-Din al-Shahid imported Ash'ari scholars like Qutb al-Din al-Naysaburi. It then addresses a group of Hanbali emigrants from Jerusalem who held anthropomorphic views inherited from Ibn Karram. Sultan Salah al-Din tolerated them because of their asceticism but did not enforce Ash'arism. The text corrects the misconception that Salah al-Din imposed Ash'arism; rather, he was lenient. It recounts an incident where Shihab al-Tusi was mistreated, and Salah al-Din's family almost adopted anthropomorphic views, but 'Izz al-Din ibn 'Abd al-Salam's firm stance defended Ash'arism, causing the opponents to retreat into their homes and limit themselves to traditional narrations.

Key Terms
أبو ذر الهروي
عبد العزيز الطبري

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Abu Dharr al-Harawi

Key Takeaway
Ash'arism first spread in Syria through direct students of al-Ash'ari and in the Hijaz through hadith transmitters.

Importation of Ash'ari Scholars by Nur al-Din
Describes importation of Ash'ari scholars by Nur al-Din.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Nur al-Din al-Shahid actively brought Ash'ari scholars to Syria to strengthen the school.

Core Idea
Rulers like Nur al-Din supported Ash'arism by importing scholars.

This lesson highlights another mechanism of Ash'ari expansion: the patronage of rulers. Nur al-Din al-Shahid, known for his piety, requested the arrival of Imam Qutb al-Din al-Naysaburi to bolster the school's presence in Syria. This shows how state support complemented scholarly networks.

Guided Path

Ash'arism was a Sunni theological school that could unify Muslims.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقام بنشر المذهب في الحجاز راوية الجامع الصحيح الحافظ ابو ذر الهروى وأخذ عنه من ارتحل اليه من علماء الآفاق، وكان انتشاره بالشام قبل ذلك بواسطة صاحب الاشعری ابی الحسن عبد العزيز الطبري راوية تفسير ابن جرير عن مؤلفه وكان اهل الشام يجتلبون عبـار الائمة من المذهب الأشعرى حيناً بعد حين كالامام قطب الدين النيسابورى اجتلبه نور الدين الشهيد على طلب العلماء. وكان جماعة من المقادسة الحنابلة ممن ورثوا بعض آراء ابن كرام الذى كان عشش بالقدس وباض وترك أصحابا له متقشفين يتوارثها منهم من بعدهم هاجروا منها لما احتلها النصارى وحملوا بدع التشبيه الى الشام وكان بها شئ من تلك البدع من عهد عبد الواحد الشيرازي صاحب أبي يعلى وكان السلطان صلاح الدين الايوبى يرعى خاطرهم لكونهم مهاجرين زهادا ويتغاضى عن معتقدهم، ولم يكن يحمل الناس علي المذهب الأشعرى كما ظن بل كان الواعظ ابن نجية الحنبلى المشهور مقربا عنده ومجافاته القاسية مع الامام الشهاب الطوسى القائم بنصرة الاشعرى بمصر تجرى على منظر منه ومسمع ويسكت عن ذلك بل كاد آله أن ينحازوا اليهم فى المعتقد لولا وقفة الأمام عز الدين بن عبد السلام فى هذه المسألة وقفة عالم يقوم بواجبه فتضاءات أصواتهم وانجمعوا في ديورهم واقتصروا على الروايات.
The spreader of the school in the Hijaz was the transmitter of the Sahih, the hafiz Abu Dharr al-Harawi, and those who traveled to him from the scholars of the regions learned from him. Its spread in Syria before that was through the companion of al-Ash'ari, Abu al-Hasan 'Abd al-'Aziz al-Tabari, the transmitter of the Tafsir of Ibn Jarir from its author. The people of Syria would import imams of the Ash'ari school from time to time, such as Imam Qutb al-Din al-Naysaburi, who was brought by Nur al-Din al-Shahid at the request of scholars. There was a group of the Muqaddasa Hanbalis who had inherited some views of Ibn Karram, who had nested in Jerusalem and bred and left ascetic followers, which they inherited from one another. They emigrated from there when the Christians occupied it and carried the innovations of anthropomorphism to Syria. There was some of that innovation in Syria from the time of 'Abd al-Wahid al-Shirazi, the companion of Abu Ya'la. Sultan Salah al-Din al-Ayyubi would consider their feelings because they were emigrants and ascetics, and he overlooked their creed. He did not compel people to follow the Ash'ari school as was thought. Rather, the preacher Ibn Najiyya al-Hanbali was close to him. And his harsh disassociation with Imam Shihab al-Tusi, who stood for the support of Ash'arism in Egypt, occurred in his sight and hearing, and he remained silent about it. Indeed, his family almost inclined towards them in creed, had it not been for the stance of Imam 'Izz al-Din ibn 'Abd al-Salam on this issue—a stance of a scholar fulfilling his duty. Then their voices faded, and they confined themselves to their homes and restricted themselves to narrations.
Source pages p. 25

Commentary
This passage continues the historical narrative, focusing on the Levant. It mentions Abu Dharr al-Harawi spreading the school in the Hijaz and 'Abd al-'Aziz al-Tabari in Syria earlier. Nur al-Din al-Shahid imported Ash'ari scholars like Qutb al-Din al-Naysaburi. It then addresses a group of Hanbali emigrants from Jerusalem who held anthropomorphic views inherited from Ibn Karram. Sultan Salah al-Din tolerated them because of their asceticism but did not enforce Ash'arism. The text corrects the misconception that Salah al-Din imposed Ash'arism; rather, he was lenient. It recounts an incident where Shihab al-Tusi was mistreated, and Salah al-Din's family almost adopted anthropomorphic views, but 'Izz al-Din ibn 'Abd al-Salam's firm stance defended Ash'arism, causing the opponents to retreat into their homes and limit themselves to traditional narrations.

Key Terms
قطب الدين النيسابوري
نور الدين الشهيد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Who brought Imam Qutb al-Din al-Naysaburi to Syria?
A) Salah al-Din al-Ayyubi
B) Nur al-Din al-Shahid
C) 'Izz al-Din ibn 'Abd al-Salam
D) Abu Dharr al-Harawi

Key Takeaway
Rulers like Nur al-Din actively imported Ash'ari scholars to strengthen the school in Syria.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The people of Syria actively imported imams. Are you actively seeking out scholars to learn from, or do you passively wait for knowledge to come to you? What specific step will you take this week to seek beneficial knowledge?
?
Nur al-Din used his authority to bring a scholar from afar. If you have any influence—even in your family or friend group—are you using it to bring people closer to sound knowledge, or are you neglecting this responsibility?
?
The scholars themselves requested the importation. When was the last time you personally requested guidance from a knowledgeable person for a specific issue in your life? If not, what holds you back?

Anthropomorphist Hanbalis and Salah al-Din's Tolerance
Describes anthropomorphist Hanbalis and Salah al-Din's tolerance.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the presence of anthropomorphist Hanbalis in Syria and Salah al-Din's tolerant stance towards them.

Core Idea
Salah al-Din tolerated anthropomorphist Hanbalis for political reasons, not because he agreed with them.

This lesson delves into a controversial group of Hanbalis who had inherited anthropomorphic ideas from Ibn Karram. They migrated from Jerusalem after the Crusader occupation and carried their beliefs to Syria. Sultan Salah al-Din, known for his justice, treated them leniently because they were ascetic refugees, but he did not adopt their creed.

Guided Path
1
Read about the Muqaddasa Hanbalis
Read the passage describing these Hanbalis and their connection to Ibn Karram.
Ibn Karram was the founder of the Karramiyya sect, known for anthropomorphism.
2
Understand Salah al-Din's stance
The passage says he 'ra'a khatirahum' (considered their feelings) and 'yataqada 'an mu'taqadihim' (overlooked their creed).
This shows tolerance, not endorsement.
3
Correct the misconception
The text explicitly says he did not force people to follow Ash'arism. Why might that be a misconception?
Some later writers claimed Salah al-Din imposed Ash'arism.

According to the passage, why did Salah al-Din tolerate the Muqaddasa Hanbalis?
A) He agreed with their creed

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Can you identify an area in your own life where you tolerate a false belief in yourself or others for the sake of convenience or comfort, just as Salah al-Din tolerated the anthropomorphists for political reasons? What would it cost you to confront it?
?
The lesson shows that even a great leader like Salah al-Din remained silent in the face of injustice against an Ash'ari advocate. Where in your relationships or work do you stay silent about something you know is wrong to avoid conflict? What is one step you can take today to speak truth?
?
The Muqaddasa Hanbalis carried harmful beliefs with them after migrating. Think about what 'baggage' you carry from your past—what beliefs or habits have you inherited that contradict the core of your faith? Are you willing to uproot them?

Ibn 'Abd al-Salam's Defense of Ash'arism
Describes Ibn 'Abd al-Salam's defense of Ash'arism.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how 'Izz al-Din ibn 'Abd al-Salam's firm stance defended Ash'arism against anthropomorphism, leading to the retreat of opposing voices.

Core Idea
One scholar's principled stand can turn the tide against heresy.

This lesson concludes the narrative with the decisive role of 'Izz al-Din ibn 'Abd al-Salam. When the sultan's family almost inclined towards anthropomorphism, Ibn 'Abd al-Salam stepped in with the courage of a scholar fulfilling his duty. His stance silenced the opponents, who then confined themselves to their homes and limited themselves to narrations.

Guided Path
1
Read the final part of the passage
Read the Arabic and translation focusing on Ibn 'Abd al-Salam's intervention.
Notice the phrase 'waqfatu 'alim yu'addi wajibahu' (stance of a scholar fulfilling his duty).
2
Identify the threat
The passage says the ruler's family almost inclined towards anthropomorphism. Who was the key protector?
Ibn 'Abd al-Salam's stance prevented this.
3
Reflect on the outcome
After his stance, the opponents' voices faded and they confined themselves. What does this tell us about the power of scholarly authority?

Life of Imam Ibn Asakir
beginner

The Importance of Ibn Asakir's Defense of Ash'ari
Praising Ibn Asakir's book and discussing the need for prepared defenses against doubts.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the significance of Ibn Asakir's book as a prepared defense against doubts and its role in preserving the Ash'ari legacy.

Core Idea
Prepared defenses in books are vital shields against creeping doubts.

In this passage, the author extols the value of having systematic defenses against doubts, pointing to Ibn Asakir's 'Tabyin Kadhib al-Muftari' as a prime example. He explains how the book refutes fabrications against Imam al-Ash'ari and compiles biographies of Ash'ari scholars, while also addressing a minor criticism about including dreams. This lesson will guide you through the key points of this methodological reflection.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and its translation
Start by reading the Arabic passage once, then the English translation. Let the author's flow settle before analyzing.
2
Identify the main purpose of the book
Notice how the passage emphasizes that the book serves as a solid barrier against doubts, accessible to both scholars and common people.
3
Examine the criticism and its context
Find where the passage discusses the inclusion of dreams. Understand the author's explanation: that the Hashwiyya prompted this, but the author believes waking proofs suffice.
Reflect on the tension between relying on dreams and rational proofs.
4
List the later works derived from Ibn Asakir's book
Scan the passage for the names of later scholars who wrote commentaries or summaries. Write them down.
These show the lasting influence of the book.
5
Reflect on the overall message
Consider why the author ends by saying there is no hope of covering all Ash'ari scholars—what does that imply about the scale of support for Sunnah?
Connects to the lesson's core idea.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
العلوم من طرائق الدفاع فى كتب خاصة بأسلوب يعلق بالخاطر وتستسيغه العامة لتكون سداً محكماً مدى الدهر دون مفاجأة جوارف الشكوك وإن لم يفعلوا ذلك يسهل على الأعداء أن يجدوا سبيلا إلى مراتع خصبة بين المسلمين تنبت فيها بذور تلبيساتهم بحيث يصعب اجتثاث عروقها الفوضوية بل تسرى سموم الالحاد في قلوب خالية تتمكن فيها فيهلك الحرث والنسل وقانا الله شر ذلك وأيقظنا من رقدتنا . هو وأحسن من قام بترجمة الامام الأشعرى وبتاريخ حياته العلمية وبيان سيرته فى الدفاع عن السنة ورد ما اختلقه خصومه عليه من ذكر تراجم مشاهير الأشاعرة الذين طبق ذكرهم الأرض من قرون متطاولة على طبقاتهم الحافظ الكبير أبو القاسم بن عساكر الدمشقي في كتابه « تبيين كذب المفترى فى ما نسب إلى الامام أبى الحسن الأشعري فله على الأشاعرة أكبر منة بذلك، ولا يزال العلماء من سالف الدهر يشكرون له هذا العمل وشهرة كتابه تغنى عن كل وصف ولا يؤخذ بشيء سوى إكثاره من ذكر رؤيا الصالحين في الموضوعات العلمية، فلعل الحشوبة هم الذين اضطروه إلى ذلك لأنهم إذا أعوزتهم الحجة فى اليقظة يلجأون إلى النوم فيجدون ما يتطلبونه من الحجج في المنام فيملأون كتبهم بالرؤى، وكان الأجدر به أن لا يعبأ بهؤلاء في ذلك، وقد كفانا مالنا من الحجج في اليقطة، وقد ذيل عليه العلامة ابن المعلم فى نجم المهتدى ورجم المعتدى) في القرن الثامن بعد أن رد على أهوازي عصره وهو كتاب حافل واختصر العفيف اليافعي کتاب ابن عساكر في كتابه الشاش المعلم ذيل المرهم وألف بعدهم كمال الدين أبو محمد بن امام الكاملية - صاحب الشمس القاياتي تلميذ العلاء البخاری ـ كتابه «طبقات الأشاعرة ) . ولا أمل في استيفائهم جميعاً في كتاب لكثرة القائمين بمناصرة السنة على طريقة الإمام الأشعرى من أهل مذاهب الأئمة الفقهاء والله الهادى .
The sciences are among the methods of defense in specific books with a style that sticks in the mind and is palatable to the common people, to be a solid barrier for all time against the sudden onslaught of doubts. If they do not do that, it becomes easy for enemies to find a way into fertile pastures among the Muslims, wherein the seeds of their deceptions sprout, such that it becomes difficult to uproot their anarchic roots; rather, the poisons of atheism spread into empty hearts where they take hold, and thus crop and progeny are destroyed—may Allah protect us from that evil and awaken us from our slumber. He is the one who best undertook the biography of Imam al-Ash'ari, the history of his scholarly life, and the exposition of his conduct in defending the Sunnah and refuting what his opponents fabricated against him, by mentioning the biographies of famous Ash'aris whose mention has filled the earth for successive centuries according to their ranks: the great hafiz Abu al-Qasim ibn 'Asakir al-Dimashqi in his book 'Tabyin Kadhib al-Muftari fima Nusiba ila al-Imam Abi al-Hasan al-Ash'ari.' So he has the greatest favor upon the Ash'aris for that, and scholars from ancient times have thanked him for this work; the fame of his book suffices for any description. Nothing is criticized except his excessive mention of the dreams of righteous people in scholarly matters. Perhaps the Hashwiyya (crude literalists) compelled him to do that, because when they lack a proof while awake, they resort to sleep and find the proofs they seek in dreams, filling their books with visions. It would have been more fitting for him not to pay attention to them in that matter, for we have sufficient proofs while awake. And al-'Allama Ibn al-Mu'allim appended a commentary to it in 'Najm al-Muhtadi wa Rajm al-Mu'tadi' in the eighth century, after he refuted the Ahwazi of his time—it is a comprehensive book. And al-'Afif al-Yafi'i summarized Ibn 'Asakir's book in his work 'al-Shash al-Mu'allam Dhayl al-Marham.' And after them, Kamal al-Din Abu Muhammad ibn Imam al-Kamilia—author of al-Shams al-Qayati, student of al-'Ala' al-Bukhari—wrote his book 'Tabaqat al-Ash'ara.' And there is no hope of covering all of them in one book because of the multitude of those who support the Sunnah according to the method of Imam al-Ash'ari from the followers of the jurisprudential imams. And Allah is the Guide.
Source pages p. 30

Commentary
This passage is a laudatory introduction to Ibn 'Asakir's 'Tabyin Kadhib al-Muftari.' It begins by emphasizing the necessity of having prepared defenses in books against doubts, using a style accessible to the common people, so that enemies cannot easily sow confusion. The author then praises Ibn 'Asakir as the best person to have written a biography of Imam al-Ash'ari, detailing his life and his defense of the Sunnah, and refuting fabrications. Ibn 'Asakir compiled biographies of famous Ash'aris over centuries. The passage notes that the only criticism of the book is its inclusion of many dreams of righteous people in scholarly matters. The author speculates that the 'Hashwiyya' (a group criticized for literalistic and uncritical acceptance of traditions) may have pressured Ibn 'Asakir to include such dreams, as they rely on dreams when lacking waking proofs. The author argues that Ibn 'Asakir should have ignored them, since sufficient waking proofs exist. The passage then lists later works based on Ibn 'Asakir's book: a commentary by Ibn al-Mu'allim, a summary by al-'Afif al-Yafi'i, and a later 'Tabaqat al-Ash'ara' by Kamal al-Din. It concludes that it is impossible to cover all Ash'ari scholars in one book due to their multitude, and praises God as the Guide.

الأشاعرة
الامام أبى الحسن الأشعري
الحشوبة
ابن المعلم
العفيف اليافعي
طبقات الأشاعرة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that including dreams in a scholarly book is always a sign of weakness or lack of evidence.
Correction: The passage explains that the inclusion of dreams was a response to the Hashwiyya who insisted on such proofs; the author himself prefers waking proofs and considers them sufficient.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the only criticism leveled against Ibn 'Asakir's book?
A) It is too long and detailed.
B) It contains excessive mention of dreams of righteous people.
C) It fails to refute the opponents of the Ash'aris.
D) It is not useful for the common people.

Key Takeaway
Ibn 'Asakir's book set a high standard for defending the Ash'ari creed, and its influence continued through later commentaries and summaries.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The passage warns that without prepared defenses, enemies can sow seeds of deception in Muslims' hearts. Are there areas of your ‘aqeedah where you feel vulnerable to doubts because you haven't studied the proofs? What specifically will you do this week to strengthen that defense?
?
Ibn ‘Asakir included dreams to appease the Hashwiyya despite having sufficient waking proofs. Have you ever softened or compromised your presentation of the truth because you feared rejection or criticism from a certain group? What would it cost you to rely solely on sound proofs from the Quran and Sunnah?
?
The author thanks God for awakening from slumber. Where in your life have you been spiritually asleep regarding the defense of the Sunnah? What concrete step will you take today to become an active defender of correct ‘aqeedah?

Life of Imam Ibn Asakir
beginner

Praise of Allah and the Prophetic Mission
Ibn 'Asakir opens with praise of Allah and describes the prophetic mission.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Ibn 'Asakir opens his work with praise of Allah and establishes the prophetic mission as a sign of Allah's grace.

Core Idea
Allah's guidance through prophets is a manifestation of His mercy.

Ibn 'Asakir begins his book with a traditional hamdalah, praising Allah for granting insights and protecting believers from doubt. He then highlights the role of prophets, especially Muhammad, as guides sent by Allah. This introduction sets the stage for discussing the deviations that later arise.

Guided Path
1
Read the opening praise
Read the Arabic passage of the hamdalah and salawat. Notice the sequence of praises and the attributes of Allah mentioned.
The hamdalah is formulaic but contains specific theological emphasis.
2
Identify the attributes of Allah
List the divine attributes mentioned in the praise, such as 'One', 'Alone', 'Praiseworthy', etc. Reflect on why these are highlighted.
3
Understand the prophetic mission
Read about how Allah chose prophets, especially Muhammad, to guide humanity. Note the language of 'destroying idols' and 'nullifying altars'.
This establishes the necessity of guidance.
4
Reflect on the purpose
Consider why Ibn 'Asakir starts with this praise. How does it prepare the reader for the discussion of deviations?
The praise affirms Allah's sovereignty and mercy before addressing errors.

بسم الله الرحمن الرحيم. الحمد لله الذي منح أهل التحقيق في توحيده بصائر وأحلاما، وشرح للتصديق بتمجيده توفيقا منه والهاما وفتح أقفال قلوبهم للإيمان به بالغيب، وكان لغيبها علاما ومسح عنها بلطفه الشك والارتياب في أمره أسقاما، أحمده على نعمه التي تظاهرت على خلقه عظاما ومننه التي تواترت من إدرار رزقه جساما، وأشهد أن لا إله إلا الله هو إلهنا أحدا فردا حمدا قدوسا سلاما قاهرا قادرا عظيما عليما خبيرا قديرا حيا قياما، وأشهد أن محمدا عبده ورسوله الذي محق به أوثانا وأصناما وأزهق ببعثته رسولا أنصابا وأزلاما، وغفر به لمن آمن بنبوته واقتدى بشريعته آصارا وآثاما وكفر في دعوته إيجابا لشفاعته ذنوبا وأجراما صلى الله عليه وعلى وصحبه ما أساغ طاعم طعاما واستعذب ظمآن شرابا والتذ مسهد مناما. أما بعد فإن الله سبحانه خص من بريته بنبوته أقواما وجعلهم على خليقته في الدعاء إلى شريعته قواما وأحكم ما شرع لهم من الدين القويم أحكاما وجعل لكل نبي منهم بالقسطاس المستقيم شرعة وأحكاما، وفرض على الأنام الاقتداء بهداهم وشرعتهم إلزاما والاقتفاء بنهجهم فيما نهجوه لهم نقضا وإبراما، واصطفى منهم محمدا صلى الله عليه وسلم وجعله للنبيين كلهم ختاما ونصبه للمتقين إماما واختار له ملة أبيه إبراهيم وسماها إسلاما وأوجب على الخلق طاعته انقيادا له واستسلاما، فجلا بنوره فجره من غياهب الشرك ظلاما، وأذهب بيقين برهانه من سباسب الشك قتاما وأسبغ به على كافة المسلمين نعمته برا بهم وإنعاما حتى أوضح لهم ما أباح حلالا وما حظر حراما فصلى الله عليه وعليهم صلوات تزداد على ممر الأوقات دواما ولقاهم يوم يلقونه في الفردوس تحية وسلاما وجزاهم الجنة بما صبروا فكم تحملوا في طاعته بمن خالفهم متاعب وآلاما وأحلهم دار المقامة بفضله وحسنت مستقرا ومقاما، ثم إن الله وله الحمد أكمل دينه وأتمه إتماما ونصب له من العلماء به أئمة يقتدي بهم وأعلاما وآتاهم بصائر نافذة عند الشبهات ورزقهم أفهاما فانتدبوا لتبصير المستبصرين حين أصبحوا متحيرين إيضاحا وإفهاما لما همى سحاب الباطل وهطل بعدما صار ركاما وقام سوق البدع عند ولاة المسلمين في الخافقين قياما وحاد أهل الاعتزال عن سنن الاعتدال جرأة منهم على رد السنن وإقداما، فنفوا عن الرب سبحانه ما أثبت لنفسه من صفاته فلم يثبتوا صفة ولا كلاما وتمادى أهل التشبيه في طرق التمويه وأحجموا عن الحق إحجاما فشبهوا ربهم حتى توهموه جسما يقبل تحيزا وافتراقا وانضماما وغلوا في إثبات كلامه حتى حسبوه يحتمل بجهلهم تجزيا وانقساما، وظنوا اسم الله القديم ألفا وهاء تتلو لاما ولاما فامتعض العلماء من المثبتين من تفاوت مذهبيهم واعتصموا بالسنة اعتصاما وألجموا العوام عن الخوض في علم الكلام خوف العثار الجاما فكان أبو الحسن الأشعري رحمة الله عليه ورضوانه أشدهم بذلك اهتماما وألدمهم لمن حاول الإلحاد في أسماء الله وصفاته خصاما وأمضاهم سنانا لمن عاند السنة وأحدهم حساما وأمضاهم جنانا عند وقوع المحنة وأصعبهم مراما ألزم الحجة لمن خالف السنة والمحجة إلزاما فلم يسرف في التعطيل ولم يغل في التشبيه وابتغى بين ذلك قواما، وألهمه الله نصرة السنة بحجج العقول حتى انتظم شمل أهلها به انتظاما وقسم الموجودات من المحدثات أعراضا وجواهر وأجساما وأثبت الله سبحانه ما أثبته لنفسه من الأسماء والصفات إعظاما ونفى عنه ما لا يليق بجلاله من شبه خلقه إجلالا له وإكراما ونزهه عن سمات الحدث تغيرا وانتقالا وإدبارا وإقبالا وأعضاء وأجراما وائتم به من وفقه الله لاتباع الحق في التمسك بالسنة ائتماما فلما انتقم من أصناف أهل البدع بإيضاح الحجج والأدلة انتقاما ووجدوه لدى الحجاج في تبيين الاحتجاج عليهم فيما ابتدعوه هماما قالوا فيه حسدا من البهتان ما لا يجوز لمسلم أن ينطق به استعظاما وقذفوه بنحو ما قذفت به اليهود عبد الله بن سلام وأباه سلاما فلم ينقصوه بذلك عند أهل التحقيق بل زادوه بما قالوا فيه تماما ومدحوه بنفس ذمهم وقد قيل في المثل لن تعدم الحسناء ذاما وقلما انفك عصر من الأعصار من غاو يقدح في
In the name of Allah, the Most Gracious, the Most Merciful. Praise be to Allah who granted the people of verification in His tawhid insights and dreams, and expanded for affirmation by glorifying Him, a success from Him and an inspiration, and opened the locks of their hearts for faith in Him through the unseen, and He was a knower of its unseen, and He wiped away from them by His kindness doubt and hesitation regarding His command, illnesses. I praise Him for His favors that have been successive upon His creation, great, and His benefactions that have been continuous from the pouring of His provision, huge. And I bear witness that there is no god but Allah, He is our God, One, Alone, Praiseworthy, Holy, Peace, Subduer, Powerful, Great, Knowing, Aware, Able, Living, Self-Subsisting. And I bear witness that Muhammad is His servant and Messenger, by whom He destroyed idols and images, and by sending him as a messenger He nullified altars and divining arrows, and by him He forgave for those who believed in his prophethood and followed his law burdens and sins, and at his call He atoned, obligating his intercession, sins and crimes. May Allah bless him and his Companions as long as a taster tastes food and a thirsty person finds drink sweet and a sleepless person enjoys sleep. To proceed: Indeed Allah, exalted, singled out from His creation by His prophethood peoples and made them, over His creation in calling to His law, leaders, and He perfected what He legislated for them of the straight religion, rulings, and He appointed for each prophet among them, with the straight balance, a law and a ruling, and He imposed upon the people following their guidance and their law as an obligation, and following their path in what they set for them, breaking and binding. And He chose from them Muhammad, peace and blessings be upon him, and made him for all the prophets a seal and appointed him for the pious as an imam, and chose for him the religion of his father Abraham and named it Islam, and obligated upon the creation obedience to him, submission and surrender to him. He revealed by his light from the depths of polytheism a darkness, and removed by the certainty of his proof from the deserts of doubt a dust, and bestowed by him upon all Muslims His favor, kindness to them and beneficence, until He clarified for them what He permitted as lawful and what He forbade as unlawful. So may Allah bless him and them with blessings that increase over the passage of time continuously, and meet them on the day they meet Him in Paradise with greeting and peace, and reward them with Paradise for what they patiently endured, for how many hardships and pains they bore in His obedience among those who opposed them, and settle them in the abode of residence by His favor, and excellent as a resting place and abode. Then indeed Allah, and to Him is praise, perfected His religion and completed it fully, and appointed for it from among the scholars leaders to be followed and signs, and gave them penetrating insights at the time of doubts and provided them with understandings, so they undertook to give insight to those seeking insight when they became perplexed, clarifying and making understand, when the cloud of falsehood poured and rained after it had become heaps, and the market of innovations stood up under the rulers of the Muslims in the two horizons, standing, and the people of i'tizal deviated from the path of moderation, out of audacity to reject the sunnah and courage, so they negated from the Lord, exalted, what He affirmed for Himself of His attributes, so they did not affirm an attribute nor speech. And the people of tashbih persisted in the ways of deception and refrained from the truth, refraining, so they likened their Lord until they imagined Him a body accepting occupying space, separation, and joining, and they exaggerated in affirming His speech until they thought, out of their ignorance, that it admits division and partition, and they thought the name of Allah, the Eternal, is alif and ha' followed by lam and lam. So the scholars of the affirmers were indignant at the disparity of their two schools, and they clung to the sunnah, clinging, and they bridled the common people from delving into the science of kalam, fearing the obstacle of stumbling. So Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari, may Allah's mercy and pleasure be upon him, was the most intense of them in that concern, and the most severe of them against those who attempted heresy regarding the names and attributes of Allah, a fighter, and the sharpest of them in spear [argument] against those who opposed the sunnah, and the sharpest of them in sword, and the most penetrating of them in mind at the time of trial, and the hardest of them in ordeal. He forced the proof against those who opposed the sunnah and the path, forcing, so he did not go to excess in negation nor did he go to excess in tashbih, and he sought between that a support. And Allah inspired him to support the sunnah with rational proofs until the unity of its people was organized through him, organized. And he divided existent things from among originated things into accidents, substances, and bodies. And he affirmed for Allah, exalted, what He affirmed for Himself of names and attributes, magnifying, and negated from Him what does not befit His majesty of likeness to His creation, exalting Him and honoring, and declared Him free from characteristics of temporality: change, movement, retreat, advance, limbs, and bodies. And those whom Allah guided to follow the truth in adhering to the sunnah followed him, following. When he took revenge on the categories of the people of innovation by clarifying proofs and evidence, revenge, and they found him at the time of argument in clarifying the proof against them regarding what they innovated, a courageous one, they said about him out of envious slander what is not permissible for a Muslim to utter, magnifying, and they accused him with something like what the Jews accused 'Abdullah ibn Salam and his father Salam with, so they did not diminish him by that among the people of verification, rather they increased him by what they said about him fully, and they praised him by the very blame of them. And it has been said in the proverb: 'The beautiful woman will not lack detractors.' And rarely is a time free from a deviator who disparages.
Source pages p. 34

Commentary
This passage is the opening of Ibn 'Asakir's book, a lengthy praise of Allah and a description of the historical context that necessitated the science of kalam, specifically the defense of Sunni theology by Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari. The passage begins with a standard hamdalah and salawat, then proceeds to 'amma ba'd' where the author explains that Allah appointed prophets, especially Muhammad, to guide humanity. He then describes how Allah completed the religion and appointed scholars as guides. However, after the early period, deviations arose: the Mu'tazila, by negating Allah's attributes and speech, and the Mushabbiha (anthropomorphists) by likening Allah to created bodies and claiming His speech is divisible into letters and sounds. Both extremes are condemned. The 'scholars of the affirmers' (al-muthbitun) – those who affirm attributes properly – restricted the common people from engaging in kalam out of fear of error. But Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari is presented as the one who undertook the defense with the utmost dedication. He did not fall into ta'til (negation) nor tashbih (likening), but took a middle path. He used rational proofs (hujaj al-'uqul) to support the sunnah. He classified created things into accidents, substances, and bodies – a standard kalam ontology. He affirmed Allah's names and attributes as Allah affirmed them, and negated anything unworthy of His majesty, such as change, movement, or body parts. The passage concludes by noting that his opponents slandered him, just as the Jews slandered 'Abdullah ibn Salam, but this only increased his honor among the people of verification. The author cites the proverb that the beautiful woman never lacks detractors, implying that the slander is a sign of Ash'ari's merit. Throughout, the author's tone is panegyric, celebrating Ash'ari as the defender of orthodoxy.

الحمد
التوحيد
النبوة
الرسالة

A) He granted them insights and opened their hearts

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read the praise of Allah in this passage, do you truly feel that your heart's 'locks' have been opened to faith in the unseen? What keeps your heart locked today, and what will you do to surrender it entirely to Him?
?
Ibn 'Asakir says through Muhammad, Allah 'destroyed idols and forgave sins.' Is there an idol in your life—a desire, a habit, a relationship—that you need to destroy so you can receive His forgiveness? What concrete step will you take today to break it?
?
The prophets were appointed as leaders and guides, and obedience to them is an obligation. In your daily decisions, are you actively following their guidance, or are you following your own whims? Which 'law' are you really obeying right now, and what needs to change?

Life of Imam Ibn Asakir
intermediate
